                return gptText.replace(/\^|\*|#|\$|\"|\'|\=|\,|\!|\+|\~|\;|\(|\)|\<|\>|\[|\]|\?|\%|\:|\@|\;|\&|\||\{|\}|\\|/g, '');
            }
            return "blank";
        }

            .setTargeting('property', 'value-of-property')    // Change and duplicate this line for as many additional keywords to send

            .setTargeting('pbPage', gptClean(gptPage))
            .setTargeting('pbSubPage', gptClean(gptSubPage))
            .setTargeting('urlpath', gptClean(document.location.pathname));

        googletag.defineSlot($GooglePublisherCategory, 'fluid', 'advert-leaderboard')

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/templates/jsp/pb2/js/plugin/thiss-ds.js" nonce="d3a30fe16b62482bbaaadfa745961b66"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="d3a30fe16b62482bbaaadfa745961b66">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '63830ad8-079d-4f9b-a0f2-61ab9f93aa85'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

        (function() {
            function riskifiedBeaconLoad() {
                var store_domain = 'https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com';
                var session_id = 'B09026350D112CC18D7AF523DF334B44';
                var url = ('https:' == document.location.protocol ? 'https://' : 'http://')
                    + "beacon.riskified.com?shop=" + store_domain + "&sid=" + session_id;
                var s = document.createElement('script');
                s.type = 'text/javascript';
                s.async = true;
                s.src = url;
                var x = document.getElementsByTagName('script')[0];
                x.parentNode.insertBefore(s, x);
            }
            if (window.attachEvent)
                window.attachEvent('onload', riskifiedBeaconLoad)
            else
                window.addEventListener('load', riskifiedBeaconLoad, false);
        })();

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d51704947" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Among various transition metal sulfides, iron-based sulfides have attracted wide attention due to their abundant resources, low cost, and non-toxicity, showing considerable research value in the field of secondary batteries. Thereinto, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> has a high theoretical specific capacity of 785 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. However, at present, the research related to Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is still in its infancy, and it also suffers from severe volume expansion and limited preparation. Therefore, to further boost its sodium storage potential, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO composite with hierarchical structure and carbonaceous network is proposed in this study. Beneficial from the ingenious hierarchitectures and flexible graphene coating, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode exhibits outstanding sodium storage performance, which can deliver a high capacity of 603 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1500 cycles with a superior capacity retention of 98%. The micron flower-like structure composed of 2D nanosheets can provide sufficient active sites and promote the rapid transport of Na<sup>+</sup>. Meanwhile, the 3D interconnected graphene carbon network makes a crucial contribution to alleviating volume changes and enhancing electrical conductivity. This work reveals the application potential of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> as an anode electrode for SIBs and provides available insights for the development of other electrode materials.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adsu202400679-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>As efficient energy storage systems, rechargeable batteries are expected to meet the growing energy demand.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0001_R_d51704939e401" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Carbon Neutraliz.">1</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) with high energy density and excellent cycling stability are the most successful commercial secondary batteries, which have been widely used in portable electronic devices and electric vehicles.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0002_R_d51704939e406" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Adv. Mater.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the scarce reserves and uneven distribution of lithium resources restrict further development of LIBs for large-scale energy storage devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0003_R_d51704939e411" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Prog. Nat. Sci. Prog. Nat. Sci.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Owing to the abundant sodium sources, low cost, and similar electrochemical properties to LIBs, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered to be the most promising candidates for next-generation grid-scale energy storage devices.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0004_R_d51704939e417" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Funct. Mater. Nat. Energy Nano Today">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To promote the development of SIBs, it is critical to explore advanced electrode materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0005_R_d51704939e422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy. Mater.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Particularly, the anode materials play an indubitable role in determining the performance of the battery.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0006_R_d51704939e428" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Energy Mater. Energy Mater.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, designing and optimizing superior anode materials to facilitate favorable sodium ion storage is still a work in progress.</p>
         
         <p>In recent years, although hard carbon (HC) anodes have shown excellent sodium storage properties, the reversible capacity of carbon-based materials is always limited, inducing low energy density of the battery.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0006_R_d51704939e436" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Energy Mater. Energy Mater.">6</a>, <a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0007_R_d51704939e436" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Environ. Sci. Adv. Funct. Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the ion diffusion kinetics of carbon-based anodes is relatively sluggish, resulting in unsatisfactory rate performance and difficulty in meeting future fast-charging requirements. Benefiting from the special storage mechanism of the conversion reaction, the transition metal sulfide anodes have both desirable reversible capacity and fast ion diffusion coefficient, which is expected to become a new generation of anode materials for SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0002_R_d51704939e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Small Adv. Mater.">2</a>, <a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0008_R_d51704939e441" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater. Carbon Neutraliz.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Among various transition metal sulfides, iron-based sulfide materials have the advantages of abundant resources, low price, and high theoretical specific capacity, meeting the needs of low-cost and high-performance SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0009_R_d51704939e446" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Energy Storage Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Currently, FeS and FeS<sub>2</sub> have been widely concerned and applied in the field of electrochemical energy storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0010_R_d51704939e454" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Alloys Compd. Adv. Fiber Mater. Carbon Adv. Energy Mater. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. Chem. Eng. J.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As for other iron-based sulfide materials, the theoretical specific capacity of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> is second only to that of FeS<sub>2</sub>, but there are few studies and reports about the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0010_R_d51704939e470" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Alloys Compd. Adv. Fiber Mater. Carbon Adv. Energy Mater. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. Chem. Eng. J.">10</a>, <a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0011_R_d51704939e470" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nanoscale">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This is mainly because Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> has fewer reserves in nature, compared with FeS and FeS<sub>2</sub>, it has received less attention and research started rather late, in turn its application in SIBs is currently in the initial stage of exploration. Besides, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> is a metastable material with poor thermal stability, which severely limits its synthesis process. However, in view of its research history, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> has shown considerable energy storage potential. For instance, Li et&nbsp;al. first applied Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> material as an anode material for SIBs and evaluated it by drawing on the relevant experience of FeS<sub>2</sub> anode. The results showed that Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode can provide a reversible specific capacity of 548 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with no significant capacity decay.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0012_R_d51704939e504" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Chem. Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, Liu et&nbsp;al. designed a flower-like Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode that can exhibit an extremely high specific capacity of 727 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0013_R_d51704939e516" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nano Energy">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Obviously, although there are a few reports on Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode, its sodium storage capability is still worthy of further exploration.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0014_R_d51704939e525" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - J. Alloys Compd. Electrochim. Acta J. Alloys Compd.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Additionally, similar to most iron-based sulfides, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> also undergoes severe volume changes caused by the conversion reaction, which seriously limits its cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0015_R_d51704939e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - J. Power Sources">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To alleviate this problem, the voltage control strategy is proposed, that is, the type of electrochemical reaction is controlled by reasonably setting the operating voltage range, and only the reaction beneficial to the performance is allowed.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0016_R_d51704939e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - J. Power Sources Energy Environ. Sci.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the higher cut-off voltage undoubtedly loses the sodium storage capacity brought by these reactions, which is inconsistent with the aim of improving energy density. Therefore, it is imperative to construct Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anodes with both outstanding capacity and stable cycle life.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0017_R_d51704939e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Energy Environ. Sci.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>Herein, we prepare Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> materials by a simple solvothermal method, which presents a 3D micron flower-like hierarchitectures assembled from 2D nanosheets. The purity and morphology of the as-prepared Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> are significantly optimized by adjusting the ratio of reactants. The 3D hierarchical Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> can cooperate with the superiority of nano and micro materials, which can not only provide multiple ion/electron diffusion channels but also maintain good structural stability. Moreover, to further improve the cycling stability, graphene coating is utilized to prepare Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO without changing the original morphology of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. The constructed 3D conductive network can effectively relieve the volume expansion arise from the conversion reaction, thereby enhancing the long-term stability. Therefore, the 3D hierarchitectures with the support of graphene conductive network endow the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode with a high specific capacity of 693 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, and even under a wide voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V, it still achieves 98% capacity retention after 1500 cycles. Driven by various optimization strategies, the sodium storage potential of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode is fully explored, which is expected to be applied in a new generation of SIBs system.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adsu202400679-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode was prepared via the one-step solvothermal method shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1a</a>, and the final product was optimized by adjusting the ratio of Fe source to S source, which is&nbsp;named as 1-1-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (Fe:S = 1:1), 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (Fe:S = 2:3) and 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (Fe:S = 1:2), respectively. First, the crystal structure of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> was characterized by X-ray diffraction (XRD). As can be seen from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1b</a>, the XRD pattern of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> can be well indexed to the pure phase Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (JCPDS No. 16–0713). There are three distinct diffraction peaks at 2<i>θ</i> = 25°, 30°, and 52°, corresponding to the (220), (311), and (440) planes of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, with almost no hybrid peaks. However, for the XRD patterns of 1-1-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> and 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, apart from the above three characteristic peaks, there is also an obvious diffraction peak at ≈2<i>θ</i> = 35°, which may be attributed to other iron-based sulfides. The reason for the appearance of the impurity phase is that in the synthesis process of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, L-cysteine needs to partially oxidize Fe<sup>2+</sup> in FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O to Fe<sup>3+</sup>, so it is easy to produce other iron-based sulfides when the addition amount is too much or too little. Therefore, XRD analysis reveals that the pure phase Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> can be successfully prepared with the ratio of Fe source and S source is 2:3. Additionally, the corresponding peaks of Fe<sup>2+</sup> and Fe<sup>3+</sup> can be clearly observed from the high-resolution X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) of Fe 2p, indicating that Fe element exists in the form of mixed-valence state, while only the peak of S<sup>2−</sup> is observed in the high-resolution S 2p spectrum, proving the successful synthesis of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> material, consistent with the XRD results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1c,d</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/aa93c288-fca3-4ea2-a292-0967d9e80664/adsu202400679-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/aa93c288-fca3-4ea2-a292-0967d9e80664/adsu202400679-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/0682fc33-84f9-46c9-a3fa-a984a1793593/adsu202400679-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/aa93c288-fca3-4ea2-a292-0967d9e80664/adsu202400679-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic illustration of preparing Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. b) XRD patterns of different Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> samples. High-resolution XPS spectra of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>: c) Fe 2p, d) S 2p. SEM images of e) 1-1-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, f) 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, g) 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. h–j) EDS mapping of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further investigate the effect of raw material ratio on the morphology of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> materials, scanning electron microscopy (SEM) was performed to characterize the microstructure of different samples (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1e–g</a>). As can be seen from Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1f</a>, the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> exhibits a 3D hierarchical micron flower-like structure composed of 2D nanosheets interspersed with each other. The size of 3D hierarchitectures is ≈5 µm, and the diameter of the nanosheets is between 1 and 3 µm. For the 1-1-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> sample, its morphology is similar to that of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1f</a>), but as the particle size increases to ≈10 µm, the nanosheets become significantly thicker (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1e</a>). Compared with the other two samples, the morphology of 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> is more irregular, consisting of abundant finely fragmented nanosheets, and the average diameter of nanosheets is less than 1 µm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1g</a>). Generally, the solvothermal reaction is usually a competitive process of crystal nucleation and growth, and the final form of the product is closely associated with the number of crystal nuclei, growth degree, assembly mode, and other factors.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0018_R_d51704939e779" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> During the synthesis of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, L-cysteine can combine with free Fe<sup>2+</sup> to form a relatively stable complex. After reaching a certain temperature, the complex decomposes to form the initial Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> crystal nucleus and gradually grows into nanosheets. As the reaction continues, these nanosheets assemble with each other and form a micron flower-like morphology. Therefore, when the amount of L-cysteine is less, the nucleation sites in the solution are also less, resulting in a tendency of continued growth of nanosheets. Ultimately, under the action of Oswald ripening, the newly generated Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> further accumulates between the nanosheets to form a thicker layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0013_R_d51704939e800" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nano Energy">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> On the contrary, when the amount of L-cysteine is more, it is easy to nucleate in large quantities and produce fragmented nanosheets, presenting the morphology of 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> samples. From the above analysis, it can be indicated that the proportion of raw materials have a significant effect on the structure and morphology of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. Thereinto, 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> with the Fe and S ratio of 2:3 has the highest purity and presents a uniform 3D flower-like hierarchitectures, which can provide large specific surface area (SSA) and short ion diffusion distance, contributing to excellent sodium storage kinetics. Besides, the energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) mapping of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0001">1h–j</a> also provides that Fe and S elements are uniformly distributed in the 3D hierarchitectures, which further proves the successful preparation of pure Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> materials.</p>
         
         <p>The sodium storage performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> was evaluated by a series of electrochemical tests. Firstly, the overall sodium storage behavior of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode in the voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V was investigated by the cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves, and the results are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information). During the first cycle, two obvious reduction peaks appear at ≈1.25 and 0.9 V, which are mainly attributed to the irreversible reduction of part of Fe<sup>3+</sup> and the formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) film. Subsequently, a reduction peak appears near 0.5 V, representing the conversion reaction of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode, which is similar to most iron-based sulfide anodes. In the follow-up process, the oxidation peaks mainly appear at 1.35 and 1.75 V, representing the extraction of sodium ions. Except for the irreversible process during the first scan, the CV curves of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> all overlap with each other, indicating that 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> has a more stable sodium storage behavior. The galvanostatic charge-discharge (GCD) profiles in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0002">2a</a> further reflect the superior storage performance of the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode. At a current density of 1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode can provide an initial discharge specific capacity of 817.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a superior initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 93%. It is also worth noting that the GCD curves of the following 20 cycles have a high degree of coincidence, and there is no significant capacity decay, indicating that the 3D flower-like Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode has excellent reversible sodium storage capability. In addition, in order to prove the compatibility between Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode and ether-based electrolyte, the sodium storage performance of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode in ester-based electrolyte was tested. It can be seen from the GCD profiles that the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode can provide an initial discharge specific capacity of 838 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> in the ester-based electrolyte, while the ICE is only 88% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0002">2b</a>). This is because the formation of SEI and the side reaction of the electrolyte bring additional irreversible capacity, but also have a serious impact on the stability of the electrode, which can be intuitively seen from the rapidly decaying capacity.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0019_R_d51704939e902" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Chem. Soc. Rev.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode delivers excellent cycling stability in the ether-based electrolyte, which is reflected by the capacity remaining at 683 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles, while in the ester-based electrolyte, the capacity decays almost to 0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0002">2c</a>). To further reveal the sodium storage behavior of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode, the rate performance test was performed (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0002">2d</a>). When the current density is 0.1, 1, 2,5,8, and 10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacity of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> is 745, 697, 669, 643, 612, and 586 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. With recovery to 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the reversible capacity returns to 743 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. Even at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode can still achieve a superior specific capacity of 500 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 500 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0002">2e</a>). Therefore, the ingenious morphology design contributes to the excellent electrochemical performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. Specifically, the large SSA of the 3D flower-like hierarchitectures can provide more active sites, while the space formed by the interpenetration of 2D nanosheets can effectively alleviate the volume expansion and promote the rapid transport of ions, thus ensuring outstanding sodium storage capacity and rate performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0020_R_d51704939e956" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Small Sci.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b3cbc94f-0a61-42c4-96d4-ace1711a1903/adsu202400679-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/b3cbc94f-0a61-42c4-96d4-ace1711a1903/adsu202400679-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e1e7d806-8571-4e36-832b-1e25f0b984b0/adsu202400679-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b3cbc94f-0a61-42c4-96d4-ace1711a1903/adsu202400679-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">GCD curves of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> in the: a) ether-based and b) ester-based electrolyte. c) The cycle performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> in different electrolytes. d) The rate performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> in the ether-based electrolyte. e) Long-term cycling performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">CV tests (scan rates is 0.2–1.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>) were performed to further reveal the superiority of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode in reaction kinetics, and the results are shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0003">3a</a>. By analyzing the scan rate (<i>v</i>, mV s<sup>−1</sup>) and peak current value (<i>i</i>, mA), the different sodium storage behavior can be reflected. Specifically, it is calculated by the following equations:

            <div class="inline-equation" id="adsu202400679-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->

         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4f3597e2-5569-42dd-9414-9e18311985ea/adsu202400679-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4f3597e2-5569-42dd-9414-9e18311985ea/adsu202400679-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/fd1b77e8-9f5f-4704-ad3d-be55183de357/adsu202400679-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4f3597e2-5569-42dd-9414-9e18311985ea/adsu202400679-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) CV curves of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> at 0.2–1.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. b) The corresponding correlations between <i>i</i> and <i>v</i>. c) Capacitive contribution at 0.6 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. d) Capacitive and diffusion contribution percentage at 0.2–1.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">The fitting value of b can be used to judge the control type of electrochemical reaction, that is, when the b value is close to 0.5, it is mainly controlled by diffusion behavior; and when the b value is close to 1, it is mainly controlled by pseudocapacitance behavior. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0003">3b</a>, the b values of almost all electrochemical reaction processes are close to 1, meaning that the processes are mainly controlled by pseudocapacitive behavior, which directly proves that the 3D flower-like Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode has fast reaction kinetics characteristics, thus can deliver excellent reversible capacity and rate performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0021_R_d51704939e1111" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Energy Mater. Adv.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, the specific contribution of pseudocapacitive behavior and diffusion behavior can be quantified:

            <div class="inline-equation" id="adsu202400679-disp-0003"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->
                  <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/75a3229b-ea5f-47d3-8b18-79c294f66879/adsu202400679-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:23667486:media:adsu202400679:adsu202400679-math-0003" display="block" location="graphic/adsu202400679-math-0003.png">
                     <semantics>
                        <mrow>
                           <mi>i</mi>
                           <mfenced close=")" open="(">
                              <mi>V</mi>
                           </mfenced>
                           <mo linebreak="badbreak">=</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi>
                              <mn>1</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <mi>v</mi>
                           <mo linebreak="goodbreak">+</mo>
                           <msub>
                              <mi mathvariant="normal">k</mi>
                              <mn>2</mn>
                           </msub>
                           <msup>
                              <mi>v</mi>
                              <mrow>
                                 <mn>1</mn>
                                 <mo>/</mo>
                                 <mn>2</mn>
                              </mrow>
                           </msup>
                        </mrow>
                        <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">$$\begin{equation}i\left( V \right) = {{{\mathrm{k}}}_1}v + {{{\mathrm{k}}}_2}{{v}^{1/2}}\end{equation}$$</annotation>
                     </semantics></math></span><span class="inline-equation__label">(3)</span></div>where k<sub>1</sub><i>v</i> and k<sub>2</sub><i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> represent the pseudocapacitive behavior contribution and diffusion behavior contribution, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0022_R_d51704939e1155" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Under the scan rates of 0.2–1.0 mV s<sup>−1</sup>, the pseudocapacitive contributions of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode are 85.4%, 87.1%, 91.1%, 94.6% and 96.7%, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0003">3c,d</a>). The dominance of pseudocapacitive charge storage can reduce the dependence on bulk diffusion, thus providing faster reaction kinetics, which explains the excellent electrochemical performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode.</div>
         
         <p>To more intuitively clarify the sodium storage behavior of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> and the evolution of the structure during the cycle, the electrodes under different states were characterized by SEM (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0004">4</a>). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0004">4a,b</a>, during the first discharge, the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode experiences significant volume expansion, that is, the original flower-like morphology transforms into a loose spherical morphology. During the charging process, the particles are refined and the surface material is partially peeled off. The same process is also experienced during the second cycle, but the material peeling is more obvious, resulting in a sharp decrease in particle size (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0004">4c,d</a>). Furthermore, with the increase of cycles, the flower-like Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> material has been refined into smaller nanoparticles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0004">4e,f</a>). This indicates that similar to most iron-based sulfide anodes, 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode also undergoes an ‘‘expansion-fracture’’ process in the voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V, which is mainly caused by the conversion reaction at low voltage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0023_R_d51704939e1210" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, it is optimized that the 3D flower-like hierarchitectures has a large interlayer space, which can effectively alleviate the volume expansion and ensure the rapid migration of ions inside the bulk phase so that most of the active materials can fully participate in the reversible conversion reaction, which is also confirmed by the change of element distribution in the EDS mapping. This also explains why 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> does not show the activation process often existing in conversion-type anode materials, presenting the phenomenon of continuous increase in capacity at the early stage of cycles, which further proves the superiority of its morphology design.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9a412fdc-aa0b-4729-a56e-ab8751814298/adsu202400679-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9a412fdc-aa0b-4729-a56e-ab8751814298/adsu202400679-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/a7c81a0d-fb56-4015-993c-642164a7b143/adsu202400679-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9a412fdc-aa0b-4729-a56e-ab8751814298/adsu202400679-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">SEM images of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode under different states: a) First fully discharged, b) First fully charged, c) Second fully discharged, d) Second fully charged, e,f) after 500 cycles.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Although the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode has shown excellent sodium storage performance, there is still a&nbsp;significant untapped opportunity for improvement in cycle stability. Considering the widely used modification strategy, carbon materials can not only provide enhanced conductivity but also protect the structural integrity of the electrode material, which can effectively improve the cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0024_R_d51704939e1250" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Mater. Chem. Front. Nano Lett.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More importantly, the graphene materials have good compatibility with the solvothermal system, and its good flexibility will not excessively destroy the original morphology of the composite.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0025_R_d51704939e1255" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Nanotechnology">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, the graphene coating strategy is selected to further improve the sodium storage performance of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode (the prepared material is named Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO). First, the microstructure of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO samples was characterized by XRD and Raman spectrum (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0005">5a,b</a>). The XRD pattern of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO sample is similar to that of 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and they match well with the standard Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> phase, indicating that the graphene-coated by solvothermal method does not destroy the microstructure of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0005">5b</a> shows the Raman spectra of the obtained samples. In addition to the response of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, the Raman spectrum of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO presents two obvious characteristic bands at ≈1345 cm<sup>−1</sup> (D-band) and 1585 cm<sup>−1</sup> (G-band), corresponding to amorphous carbon and graphite carbon, respectively.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0026_R_d51704939e1314" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This significant difference is further evidence of the successful preparation of graphene-coated Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> materials. The SEM and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) were utilized to characterize the morphology and element distribution of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO. From the SEM images (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0005">5c,d</a>), it can be clearly observed that the film-like graphene is covered on the surface of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> material, consistent with the TEM result (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0005">5e</a>). Interestingly, the flower-like morphology of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> becomes more irregular, which is because the addition of graphene affects the complexation of Fe<sup>2+</sup> and L-cysteine, thus limiting the growth of micro flowers to a certain extent. Moreover, the EDS mapping of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO presents that C is homogenously distributed in the whole material, while Fe and S are concentrated in Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> hierarchitectures (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0005">5f–h</a>). These analyses indicate that a better graphene coating effect is achieved by solvothermal method, and the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode with favorable morphology is prepared.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/9c749dbe-eb26-41c1-8e96-045c06d3ed89/adsu202400679-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/9c749dbe-eb26-41c1-8e96-045c06d3ed89/adsu202400679-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/c85315c1-18c6-4919-b0b9-9b098431a55a/adsu202400679-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/9c749dbe-eb26-41c1-8e96-045c06d3ed89/adsu202400679-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) XRD patterns and b) Raman spectra of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO and 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. c,d) SEM, and e) TEM images of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO. f–h) EDS mapping of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <div class="paragraph-element">Electrochemical performances were investigated by the GCD measurements (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0006">6a</a>). In the wide voltage range of 0.01–3.0 V, there is almost no capacity attenuation from the GCD curves except for the first cycle, indicating that Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode has outstanding reversible sodium storage capability. In terms of rate performance, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode can provide reversible capacities of 718, 693, 659, 613, 580, and 548 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at current densities of 0.1–10 A g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0006">6b</a>). Furthermore, as the current density returns to 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, its reversible capacity also recovers to 726 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>. In particular, at a current density of 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode can still deliver an excellent specific capacity of 603 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1500 cycles with a high capacity retention of 98% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0006">6c</a>). Compared with the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode, the cyclic stability of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO has been significantly improved, which means that graphene can effectively maintain the structure stability by buffering the volume expansion, and the formed 3D conductive network can promote the rapid transport of ions and electrons. To evaluate the sodium storage kinetics of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode in more detail, the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) tests were performed on the cells under the open circuit voltage (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0006">6d</a>). In a typical Nyquist plot, the arc in the high-frequency region reflects the charge transfer impedance (<i>R<sub>ct</sub></i>), while the straight line in the low-frequency region reflects the ion diffusion impedance (<i>R<sub>W</sub></i>). Using the equivalent circuit model shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adsu202400679-fig-0006">6d</a> to fit the Nyquist plots, it can be obtained that the <i>R<sub>ct</sub></i> of the 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode is ≈4.23 Ω, while the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode is only 1.79 Ω, which shows that graphene can remarkably enhance the charge transfer ability, thus ensuring the rapid and stable electrochemical reaction. In addition, based on the analysis of EIS, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<i>D<sub>Na</sub>+</i>) can be calculated according to the following equations:

         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adsu202400679-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/7003df44-4861-4aa4-8e21-846ea74b9e8e/adsu202400679-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/7003df44-4861-4aa4-8e21-846ea74b9e8e/adsu202400679-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/96dccae9-d7b9-416d-bbfa-b3c017fc6de6/adsu202400679-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/7003df44-4861-4aa4-8e21-846ea74b9e8e/adsu202400679-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adsu202400679-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadsu.202400679" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) GCD curves of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO. b) The rate performance of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO. c) Long-term cycling performance of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>. d) EIS plots and the equivalent circuit model of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO and 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. e) Linear relationship between ω<sup>−0.5</sup> and Z<sub>re</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further illustrate the function of graphene coating on cycling stability, the surface state of the electrode after long-term cycles was characterized. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information), after 500 cycles, cracks of 1–5 µm can be observed everywhere on the surface of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode, while the surface of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO remains intact with almost no cracks appearing. Obviously, the carbon network formed by the interconnected graphene can not only alleviate the stress caused by volume expansion but also anchor Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> material inside the carbon layer to prevent it from falling off, thus endowing Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO with excellent structural stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0028_R_d51704939e1690" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Chem. Eng. J.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, with the ingenious 3D hierarchitectures design and the help of graphene coating, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode exhibits superior sodium storage performance compared with the existing studies, as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> (Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0010_R_d51704939e1703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - J. Alloys Compd. Adv. Fiber Mater. Carbon Adv. Energy Mater. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. J. Colloid Interface Sci. Chem. Eng. J. Chem. Eng. J.">10</a>-<a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0013_R_d51704939e1703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Nano Energy">13</a>, <a href="#adsu202400679-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adsu202400679-bib-0029_R_d51704939e1703" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - J. Power Sources">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adsu202400679-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, a 3D hierarchical flower-like Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode is prepared by a simple one-step hydrothermal method, and its electrochemical properties are further optimized by the graphene coating strategy. The 3D hierarchitectures assembled by 2D nanosheets can ensure shorter diffusion channels for ions and electrons, and provide numerous active sites. Moreover, the flexible graphene layer can uniformly anchor Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> on the carbon layer to effectively buffer volume expansion, and the formed conductive network can enhance the overall conductivity of the material. As a result, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anodes exhibit impressive sodium storage performance. Particularly, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> anode delivers a high initial discharge capacity of 817.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with relatively high ICE of 93%. Furthermore, with the assistance of graphene, the Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO still own a capacity retention of up to 98% after 1500 cycles. Therefore, this work not only paves the way for the application of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> materials for the new generation of SIBs, but the proposed insights can also be extended to the development of other advanced electrode materials.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adsu202400679-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adsu202400679-sec-0070-title"> Material Preparation</h4>
                  
                  <p>The preparation process of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> was as follows: 2 mmol ferrous sulfate heptahydrate (FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O) and 3 mmol L-cysteine (C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>7</sub>NO<sub>2</sub>S) were dissolved in 40 mL deionized water and stirred at 500 rpm for 5 min. Subsequently, the FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O solution was slowly poured into the C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>7</sub>NO<sub>2</sub>S solution under continuous stirring, and the stirring was continued at 500 rpm for 20 min until the solution was clarified. After stirring, the solution was transferred to a 100 mL reactor tank and then placed in a Memmert UN55 oven at 180 °C for 12 h. After natural cooling, the obtained solution and precipitate were transferred to a centrifuge tube, washed twice with deionized water, and then washed three times with anhydrous ethanol. The centrifugal speed was 10&nbsp;000 rpm and the centrifugal time was 5 min. Finally, the obtained product was transferred to a vacuum oven and dried overnight at 80 °C to obtain Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> black powder. The amount of Fe source and S source added in the above steps was 2 and 3 mmol, respectively, so the sample was recorded as 2-3-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. In addition, the samples prepared when the amount of Fe source and S source was 2 and 2 mmol were recorded as 1-1-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>, and the samples prepared when the amount of Fe source and S source was 2 and 4 mmol were recorded as 1-2-Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>.</p>
                  
                  <p>The preparation process of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO anode material was as follows: 2 mmol FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O and 3 mmol C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>7</sub>NO<sub>2</sub>S were dissolved in 35 mL deionized water, respectively. The FeSO<sub>4</sub>·7H<sub>2</sub>O solution was poured into the C<sub>3</sub>H<sub>7</sub>NO<sub>2</sub>S solution and stirred for 20 min, then 10 mL graphene oxide dispersion (5 mg mL<sup>−1</sup>) was slowly dripped into the mixed solution with a dropper, and the stirring was continued for 30 min. The subsequent solvothermal process was the same as that of Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>. The speed of centrifugal cleaning was changed to 2000 rpm to prevent the separation of graphene from the material. After drying, Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO black powder was obtained.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adsu202400679-sec-0080-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The crystal structures of as-prepared were characterized by XRD. The element valence of the material was analyzed by XPS. To ensure the successful coating of graphene, the material was characterized by Raman spectroscopy. The microstructure of the material was observed by SEM and TEM. The EDS was used to analyze the element distribution of the material.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adsu202400679-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adsu202400679-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <p>All the electrochemical properties were tested using CR2022-type coin cells. The slurry was prepared by mixing Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub> powder (or Fe<sub>3</sub>S<sub>4</sub>@rGO powder), conductive carbon black, and binder (CMC-Na) in a mass ratio of 7:2:1. The slurry was evenly coated on the copper foil with a 100 µm scraper, and placed in a vacuum oven to dry at 80°C for one night. After drying, it was cut into 11 mm diameter discs. The CR2025 coin cell was assembled in a glove box (MBRAUN, LabStar, O<sub>2</sub>&lt;0.01&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−6</sup>, H<sub>2</sub>O&lt;0.01&nbsp;×&nbsp;10<sup>−6</sup>), using the ether-based electrolyte (1.0 <span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in Diglyme) and the ester-based electrolyte (1.0 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in EC and DEC with a volume ratio of 1:1). The galvanostatic charge-discharge (GCD) and rate capability were carried out using Land CT2001A battery tester system. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) and electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) were carried out on the electrochemical workstation (CHI660E). The voltage range of all tests was 0.01–3.0 V, and the EIS was tested at open circuit voltage.</p>
                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
